## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through constitutive laws (linear or nonlinear elasticity, plasticity) and on temperature through thermal softening, thermal activation, or phase-dependent modulus changes.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain in plastic regime)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (flow stress with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening linear: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (exponentially decaying stiffness with temperature)
- Neo-Hookean rubber elasticity: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * epsilon**3) (entropic elasticity in polymers/rubbers)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (general nonlinear elasticity)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with thermal dependence)
- Ludwik-Hollomon with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal factor)
- Hyperbolic sine flow rule: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (thermally activated deformation)
- Entropic rubber elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (stress proportional to T*strain for ideal rubber)
- Sigmoidal stress-strain: sigma = c0 / (1 + exp(c1 * (c2 - epsilon))) * (c3 + c4 * T) (S-shaped stress-strain with thermal factor)
- Combined power-exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 + c3 * T + c4 * T**2) (power-law strain with polynomial temperature dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Entropic elasticity (rubber/polymer) → Stress proportional to temperature: sigma ~ T * f(epsilon), indicating entropy-driven restoring force
- Thermal softening in metals → Multiplicative factor (1 - (T/Tm)^c) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: sigma ~ c*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), Voce-type saturation
- Power-law plastic flow → sigma ~ epsilon^n with n < 1 (work hardening exponent), common in metals beyond yield
- Temperature-modulus coupling → Elastic modulus E(T) appears as a prefactor: sigma = E(T)*g(epsilon), separable form
- Strain stiffening in biological/polymeric materials → Exponential or sinh dependence: sigma ~ exp(c*epsilon) - 1
- Phase transition or glass transition → Abrupt change in stress-strain slope at critical temperature, piecewise or tanh-based switching in T
- Small strain linearity transitioning to nonlinearity → Leading linear term plus higher-order corrections: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon^3
